\id Paderina_Egorova_razgovor_000_metadata
\ref Recorded on 07 July 2009 in Esso by Natalia Aralova and Brigitte Pakendorf. The recording was undertaken in the kitchen of the
house that BP and NA are renting in Esso. It had been arranged beforehand with RME, who'd invited her friend JIP. RME is our
primary consultant and very much used to speaking with a microphone in front of her; JIP at first got a bit of a fright, but was able to
uphold the conversation - which is mainly RME speaking, anyway.  We'd laid the table with some things for tea, and then withdrew to
other rooms to let the two women chat in as natural a setting as possible. There are some noises from the street, and unfortunately
we'd forgotten to switch off the fridge, which came on in the middle.
\qu Transcription and Russian translation in Word by Rimma Maksimovna Egorova, time-aligned in ELAN by Luise Zippel, glossing by BP (2016).
Funding by the Volkswagen Foundation (DoBeS grant) and CNRS/Universit� Lyon 2 (laboratoire DDL). Speaker abbreviations = JIP, RME
\ref Julia Ivanovna Paderina (Solodikova) was born in 1950, i.e. she was 59-60 at the time of recording. She has a college-level education
and worked as radio-operator. Professed herself as being better in Russian than in Even, speaks Russian with children.
\ref Rimma Maksimovna Egorova was born in 1954, i.e. she was 54-55 at the time of the recording. She has a college-level education and
had variously worked as the person who projects movies, a junior nurse, and as a cleaner in the post office as well as doing the
laundry in the old people's home. She is married to a Russian. She is the sister of Raisa Maksimovna Solodikova.

"postojanno idite v shkolu" = urgerelle, or olloːtkerelle; tiːwdʒis = u vas otberut, vy stradaete tem, chto ot vas otberut; and one could say: "vdrug tala tiːwʤikes" (but
this is 2sg), tiːwʤikelšen = OK; "vdrug tala tiːʤikelšen" = a to vy otberete; tiːwʤikelsen = a vdrug otberut; tiːwʤis = odnokratno, vdrug otberut; tiːwʤikelsen =
otbiratj budut --- which makes it seem as if there's an aspectual distinction

\gr kučukešteken = po-menshe; abalšakan = po-menshe; nọːdšukan = bolee krasivo; milterešuken uŋkeli = po-polnee nalivaj; *kučukeš = netu; egʤešuken, egʤešteken;

\gr 06/06/2016: kučukešeken = kučukešteken = kučukenšuken; Q: nọːštakan (nọːdšukan) A: what is nọːštakan? no; ŋuleńešteken = NO - ŋuleńešuken; ewešišteken mičille
(instead of eweškišuken) = no; kučukešteken seems to be a synonym only of kučukenšuken, it doesn't seem to be a productive suffix
\gr 11/06/2016: while merging databases I found the attenuative suffixe -stE, which I think is the one in kočukešteken, so I wanted to check whether this occurs with other
roots: ŋuleńešte rubaxa = krasnovataja, da mozhno; nọːdešte aši ? (I thought of "a somewhat pretty woman) - this she changed to nọːdešte nọŋandukun = bolee
krasivaja chem ona - so it seems to function exactly like -sukEn
\nt
